Karramiyya on Divine Attributes: Two Subgroup Views
Nasafi presents two Karramiyya subgroups and their opposing doctrines on divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two opposing views within the Karramiyya on whether God's attributes include meta-attributes like 'alimiyya, and why the author rejects one of them.

Core Idea
The Karramiyya disagreed whether God is knowing by 'knowingness' or by knowledge itself.

This passage examines two subgroups within the Karramiyya on the nature of divine attributes. One group affirms that God is knowing by knowledge, but denies that He is knowing by a distinct meta-attribute called 'knowingness'. The other group affirms such meta-attributes, leading to what the author considers a grave error. Let us explore their arguments and the author's critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the first subgroup's view
Read the passage about the first subgroup and note their claim: God is knowing by knowledge, powerful by power, living by life, but not by 'knowingness' etc.
They reason that 'knowingness' would be a power over knowledge, which is not under power.
2
Understand the first subgroup's reasoning
Consider why 'knowingness' cannot be conceived: knowledge, power, and life are not subject to being created or controlled, so a meta-attribute over them is impossible.
3
Read the second subgroup's view
Read the passage about the second subgroup and note their affirmation: they posit 'creatorship' as distinct from power, and similarly 'knowingness' etc. as separate meanings.
4
Note the author's condemnation
The author calls this view 'utmost stupidity and misguidance'. Understand why: it makes God knowing by something other than knowledge, which is incoherent.
5
Compare the two views
Contrast the two positions: one sticks to known attributes, the other adds meta-attributes. Which one is more coherent according to the author?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهؤلاء يقولون : إنه عالم بعلمه وقادر بقدرته وحي بحياته، ولا يقولون هو عالم بعالميته وقادر بقادريته وحي بحييته لما أن العالمية والقادرية والحيية قدرة على العلم والقدرة والحياة، وهذا الصفات لا تدخل تحت القدرة، فلا يتصور عالميته ولا قادريته ولا حييته. ومنهم من قال : الخالقية معنى مخصوص به يكون الخالق خالقا وهي غير القدرة، ويقولون : إنه عالم بعالمية وقادر بقادرية وحي بحيية، وهذه المعاني غير القدرة والعلم والحياة. فيجعلونه عالما قادرا حيا بما ليس بعلم ولا قدرة ولا حياة، ولا يجعلونه عالما قادرا حيا بالعلم والقدرة والحياة. وهذا غاية الغباوة والضلالة. ثم بينهم اختلاف في جواز عدم ما حدث في ذاته من المعاني منهم من جوز ذلك، وهذا هو القول بالتغير، ومنهم من لم يجوز ذلك وهو القول باستحالة العدم على الحوادث، وكلا القولين باطل.
And these (subgroup) say: He is knowing by His knowledge, powerful by His power, living by His life, and they do not say He is knowing by His 'knowingness' ('alimiyya), powerful by His 'powerfulness' (qadiriyya), and living by His 'livingness' (hayyiyya), because 'knowingness', 'powerfulness', and 'livingness' are power over knowledge, power, and life, and these attributes do not fall under power, so His 'knowingness', 'powerfulness', and 'livingness' cannot be conceived. And among them is one who said: 'Creatorship' (khaliqiyya) is a specific meaning by which the Creator is Creator, and it is other than power; and they say: He is knowing by 'knowingness', powerful by 'powerfulness', and living by 'livingness', and these meanings are other than power, knowledge, and life. So they make Him knowing, powerful, living by that which is not knowledge, power, nor life, and they do not make Him knowing, powerful, living by knowledge, power, and life. This is the utmost stupidity and misguidance. Then among them there is disagreement regarding the permissibility of nonexistence (adam) of what occurred in His essence of the meanings: from among them, one permitted that—and this is the statement of change (taghayyur)—and from among them, one did not permit it—and this is the statement of the impossibility of nonexistence upon temporal events. Both statements are false.
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage discusses two subgroups within the Karramiyya on the issue of divine attributes. One subgroup affirms that God is knowing by knowledge, powerful by power, living by life, but denies that God is knowing by 'knowingness' ('alimiyya), etc. Their reason is that 'knowingness', 'powerfulness', and 'livingness' would be powers over knowledge, power, and life respectively, but these (knowledge, power, life) are not subject to power (i.e., cannot be created), so such powers cannot be conceived. Thus they reduce the attributes to the standard ones (knowledge, power, life) without accepting meta-attributes like 'knowingness'. Another subgroup posits that 'creatorship' (khaliqiyya) is a distinct meaning besides power, and similarly they affirm 'knowingness', etc., as realities other than knowledge, power, and life. The author condemns this second view as utter stupidity and misguidance because it affirms attributes that are not knowledge, power, or life, yet make God knowing, powerful, living through them. Then the author notes an internal disagreement among the Karramiyya: whether the temporal events that occur in God's essence (as per their doctrine) can cease to exist. Some allow cessation (the view of change, taghayyur), others deny it (the view that temporal events cannot cease). The author declares both positions false.

Key Terms
عالمية
قادرية
حيية
خالقية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that affirming 'knowingness' as a separate attribute is harmless and adds depth to divine attributes.
Correction: The author shows it leads to the absurdity that God is knowing by something other than knowledge, which undermines the very meaning of 'knowing'.

Checkpoint
According to the first Karramiyya subgroup, why is it inconceivable for God to be knowing by 'alimiyya (knowingness)?
A) Because 'alimiyya would be a power over knowledge, and knowledge is not subject to power.
B) Because 'alimiyya is a created attribute.
C) Because God does not have knowledge.
D) Because 'alimiyya is synonymous with knowledge.

Key Takeaway
The first subgroup maintains that God's attributes are knowledge, power, and life themselves, and denies meta-attributes, while the second subgroup affirms them but is condemned for making God knowing without knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of Allah's knowledge, do you ever treat it as a separate 'thing' that He possesses, rather than as an essential part of who He is? How would your trust in His omniscience change if you fully internalised that His knowledge is not an addition but His very self? Will you pause today—even for a moment—to reflect on the difference and let it deepen your reverence?
?
The passage condemns making Allah knowing by something other than knowledge as 'utmost stupidity and misguidance.' Where in your own understanding of Allah might you have added invented concepts that distance you from the simple truth of His attributes? Are you willing to surrender your own philosophical constructions and accept what revelation teaches, even if it feels less sophisticated?
?
If you were to explain to someone why affirming 'knowingness' as a separate attribute is incoherent, would you be speaking from mere intellectual knowledge or from a heart that has tasted the reality of Allah's attributes? Which of the two subgroups' attitudes reflects your current state: content with what is revealed, or prone to overcomplicating? This week, commit to resisting the urge to add to Allah's description.

Karramiyya Internal Dispute on Change and Non-Existence
Nasafi reports an internal Karramiyya disagreement on whether temporal attributes in God's essence can cease.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the internal disagreement among the Karramiyya regarding whether the temporal meanings in God's essence can cease to exist, and why both positions are deemed false.

Core Idea
The Karramiyya internal dispute on change: can God's temporal attributes vanish? Both answers are wrong.

After discussing the two camps on attribute realities, Nasaﬁ turns to a related internal disagreement: whether the temporal events that occur in God's essence (according to Karramiyya doctrine) can cease to exist. Some say yes (change), others no (impossibility of ceasing). The author dismisses both.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on internal disagreement
Read the short passage about the disagreement among the Karramiyya regarding the possibility of non-existence of the meanings that occur in God's essence.
2
Identify the two positions
One position permits non-existence (change, taghayyur), the other forbids it (impossibility of non-existence, istihalat al-'adam).
3
Understand the term 'change'
Those who permit non-existence are said to hold the view of change (taghayyur) in God's essence. Reflect on why that would be problematic.
Change in God is generally denied in Islamic theology.
4
Understand the term 'impossibility of non-existence'
Those who deny that the meanings can cease hold that temporal events cannot disappear. This also raises issues about God's essence having temporal events that are permanent.
5
Note the author's dismissal
The author declares both statements false. Consider why both are unacceptable from a sound theological perspective.
Both positions lead to absurdities about God's essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهؤلاء يقولون : إنه عالم بعلمه وقادر بقدرته وحي بحياته، ولا يقولون هو عالم بعالميته وقادر بقادريته وحي بحييته لما أن العالمية والقادرية والحيية قدرة على العلم والقدرة والحياة، وهذا الصفات لا تدخل تحت القدرة، فلا يتصور عالميته ولا قادريته ولا حييته. ومنهم من قال : الخالقية معنى مخصوص به يكون الخالق خالقا وهي غير القدرة، ويقولون : إنه عالم بعالمية وقادر بقادرية وحي بحيية، وهذه المعاني غير القدرة والعلم والحياة. فيجعلونه عالما قادرا حيا بما ليس بعلم ولا قدرة ولا حياة، ولا يجعلونه عالما قادرا حيا بالعلم والقدرة والحياة. وهذا غاية الغباوة والضلالة. ثم بينهم اختلاف في جواز عدم ما حدث في ذاته من المعاني منهم من جوز ذلك، وهذا هو القول بالتغير، ومنهم من لم يجوز ذلك وهو القول باستحالة العدم على الحوادث، وكلا القولين باطل.
And these (subgroup) say: He is knowing by His knowledge, powerful by His power, living by His life, and they do not say He is knowing by His 'knowingness' ('alimiyya), powerful by His 'powerfulness' (qadiriyya), and living by His 'livingness' (hayyiyya), because 'knowingness', 'powerfulness', and 'livingness' are power over knowledge, power, and life, and these attributes do not fall under power, so His 'knowingness', 'powerfulness', and 'livingness' cannot be conceived. And among them is one who said: 'Creatorship' (khaliqiyya) is a specific meaning by which the Creator is Creator, and it is other than power; and they say: He is knowing by 'knowingness', powerful by 'powerfulness', and living by 'livingness', and these meanings are other than power, knowledge, and life. So they make Him knowing, powerful, living by that which is not knowledge, power, nor life, and they do not make Him knowing, powerful, living by knowledge, power, and life. This is the utmost stupidity and misguidance. Then among them there is disagreement regarding the permissibility of nonexistence (adam) of what occurred in His essence of the meanings: from among them, one permitted that—and this is the statement of change (taghayyur)—and from among them, one did not permit it—and this is the statement of the impossibility of nonexistence upon temporal events. Both statements are false.
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage discusses two subgroups within the Karramiyya on the issue of divine attributes. One subgroup affirms that God is knowing by knowledge, powerful by power, living by life, but denies that God is knowing by 'knowingness' ('alimiyya), etc. Their reason is that 'knowingness', 'powerfulness', and 'livingness' would be powers over knowledge, power, and life respectively, but these (knowledge, power, life) are not subject to power (i.e., cannot be created), so such powers cannot be conceived. Thus they reduce the attributes to the standard ones (knowledge, power, life) without accepting meta-attributes like 'knowingness'. Another subgroup posits that 'creatorship' (khaliqiyya) is a distinct meaning besides power, and similarly they affirm 'knowingness', etc., as realities other than knowledge, power, and life. The author condemns this second view as utter stupidity and misguidance because it affirms attributes that are not knowledge, power, or life, yet make God knowing, powerful, living through them. Then the author notes an internal disagreement among the Karramiyya: whether the temporal events that occur in God's essence (as per their doctrine) can cease to exist. Some allow cessation (the view of change, taghayyur), others deny it (the view that temporal events cannot cease). The author declares both positions false.

Checkpoint
What is the view called that permits the non-existence of temporal meanings in God's essence?
A) استحالة العدم
B) التغير
C) القادرية
D) العالمية

Key Takeaway
The Karramiyya were divided on whether the temporal meanings in God's essence could cease, but both views are rejected as false.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine God's involvement in the world, do you ever secretly feel that He must 'change' to respond to new situations? This passage warns against that. What in your heart needs to be retrained to trust that God's essence remains unchanging while still being perfectly responsive?
?
Both Karramiyya groups fell into error because they tried to explain the unexplainable. Are there aspects of God's nature that you feel uncomfortable leaving as a mystery? What would it cost you to humbly accept the limits of your intellect before the Creator?

The Karramiyya Doctrine on Accidents in God's Essence
Nasafi reports the Karramiyya claim of accidents in God's essence and the majority subgroup's view on attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Karramiyya claim that accidents occur in God's essence and their distinction between eternal powers and temporal acts.

Core Idea
The Karramiyya attribute temporal events to God's essence while denying they imply change.

Nasafi presents the controversial Karramiyya position that God's essence becomes a locus for originated events like hearing and seeing. They attempt to preserve God's eternity by distinguishing between eternal powers (like speaker-power) and temporal acts (like speech). This lesson explains their core doctrine before exploring internal disagreements.

Guided Path
1
Read the Karramiyya claim about accidents
Read the first part of the passage where Nasafi describes how the Karramiyya say touching, seeing, and hearing occur in God's essence. Notice the distinction they make between eternal powers (like hearing-power) and the temporal acts themselves.
The Karramiyya attempt to avoid saying God changes by positing eternal capacities.
2
Understand the distinction between powers and acts
The passage explains that God is called 'Hearing' in pre-eternity not by an eternal hearing but by a hearing-power, while the actual hearing occurs when He hears. Similarly for speaking and creating. Identify each pair of power and act.
3
Identify the first subgroup's position on attributes
After describing the main doctrine, Nasafi states that the majority of the Karramiyya affirm that God is knowing by knowledge, powerful by power, and living by life. They reject the idea of powers over these attributes (like knowing-power), arguing that such powers would be over things not subject to power.
This subgroup avoids the infinite regress of powers over powers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
محدثات العالم. وكذا قالوا بحدوث مماسة في ذاته عند مماسته لما يماس من الأجسام، وكذا عند رؤيته شيئا أو سماعه صوتا يحدث فيه تسمع وتبصر المبصرات والمرئيات ويسمونه سميعا في الأزل لا بسمع قائم بذاته بل بسمعيته [بعدد؟] يعنون به قدرته على السمع، وكذا يسمونه بصيرا ببصريته، ثم تبصره وتسمعه محدثان، وكذا كان في الأزل متكلما قائلا لا بقوله وكلامه بل بقائليته ومتكلميته، وهما قدرته على القول والكلام، فأما الكلام فهو يحدث عند تكلمه. وكذا كان في الأزل خالقا بخالقيته ورازقا برازقيته، وهما القدرة على الرزق وعلى الخلق، فأما الخلق والرزق فهما يحدثان في ذاته. هذا هو مذهب جمهورهم وهؤلاء يقولون : إنه عالم بعلمه وقادر بقدرته وحي بحياته، ولا يقولون هو عالم بعالميته وقادر بقادريته وحي بحييته لما أن العالمية والقادرية والحيية قدرة على العلم والقدرة والحياة، وهذا الصفات لا تدخل تحت القدرة، فلا يتصور عالميته ولا قادريته ولا حييته. ومنهم من قال : الخالقية معنى مخصوص به يكون الخالق خالقا وهي غير القدرة، ويقولون : إنه عالم بعالمية وقادر بقادرية وحي بحيية، وهذه المعاني غير القدرة والعلم والحياة. فيجعلونه عالما قادرا حيا بما ليس بعلم ولا قدرة ولا حياة، ولا يجعلونه عالما قادرا حيا بالعلم والقدرة والحياة. وهذا غاية الغباوة والضلالة. ثم بينهم اختلاف في جواز عدم ما حدث في ذاته من المعاني منهم من جوز ذلك، وهذا هو القول بالتغير، ومنهم من لم جوز ذلك وهو القول باستحالة العدم على الحوادث، وكلا القولين باطل.
The originated things of the world. And likewise they said: the occurrence of touching in His essence when He touches what He touches of bodies, and likewise when He sees something or hears a sound, there occurs in Him hearing and seeing of the seen and visible things, and they call Him 'Hearing' in pre-eternity not by a hearing subsisting in His essence but by His hearing-power, intending thereby His power over hearing. And likewise they call Him 'Seeing' by His seeing-power, then His seeing and His hearing are originated. And likewise He was in pre-eternity a Speaker, a Sayer, not by His speech and His word but by His sayer-power and His speaker-power, and they are His power over speech and speaking. As for speech, it occurs when He speaks. And likewise He was in pre-eternity a Creator by His creator-power and a Provider by His provider-power, and they are the power over provision and over creation. As for creation and provision, they occur in His essence. This is the doctrine of the majority of them. And these say: He is knowing by His knowledge, powerful by His power, living by His life, and they do not say He is knowing by His knowing-power, powerful by His power-power, living by His living-power, because knowing-power, power-power, and living-power are power over knowledge, power, and life, and these attributes do not fall under power, so His knowing-power, power-power, and living-power are inconceivable. And among them is one who said: Creator-power is a particular meaning by which the Creator is Creator, and it is other than power. And they say: He is knowing by a knowing-power, powerful by a power-power, living by a living-power, and these meanings are other than power, knowledge, and life. Thus they make Him knowing, powerful, living by what is not knowledge, power, nor life, and they do not make Him knowing, powerful, living by knowledge, power, and life. And this is the extreme of stupidity and misguidance. Then among them there is disagreement concerning the permissibility of the non-existence of what occurred in His essence of the meanings: some permitted that, and this is the doctrine of change; and some did not permit that, and this is the doctrine of the impossibility of non-existence for originated things. And both doctrines are false.
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the Karramiyya doctrine regarding God's attributes. The author first describes their view: they claim that temporal events (ḥawādith) occur in God's essence, such as when He touches bodies, sees something, or hears a sound, then hearing and seeing come to be in Him. They distinguish between eternal attributes of 'hearing-power' (samʿiyya) and 'seeing-power' (baṣariyya) and the actual acts of hearing and seeing which are originated. They similarly hold that God is eternally a Speaker not by an eternal speech but by a speaker-power (qāʾiliyya, mutakallimiyya), while actual speech occurs when He speaks. Likewise, God is eternally a Creator by a creator-power (khāliqiyya) and a Provider by a provider-power (rāziqiyya), while creation and provision occur in His essence. The author then distinguishes two sub-groups among them: the majority affirm that God is knowing by knowledge, powerful by power, and living by life; they reject the notion of 'knowing-power' (ʿālamiyya), 'power-power' (qādariyya), and 'living-power' (ḥayyiyya) because these would be powers over attributes that cannot be subject to power. Another sub-group, however, affirms such powers as distinct entities beyond knowledge, power, and life, attributing to God knowledge and power and life through these instead of through the attributes themselves—a view the author calls extreme stupidity and misguidance. Finally, the author notes that the Karramiyya themselves disagree about the permanence of these originated meanings in God: some allow them to cease (which implies change in God), others deny their cessation (which implies the impossibility of non-existence for originated things). The author declares both positions false.

Key Terms
محدثات
مماسة
سمعية
بصرية
قائلية
متكلمية
خالقية
رازقية
عالمية
قادرية
حيية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the Karramiyya simply believe that God undergoes change or has temporal attributes like creatures.
Correction: The Karramiyya try to avoid implying change by distinguishing between eternal powers (which are not accidents) and temporal acts (which are accidents occurring in God's essence). However, this still contradicts God's immutability.

Checkpoint
According to the Karramiyya, what does God have in pre-eternity that allows Him to be called 'Hearing'?
A) An eternal hearing attribute subsisting in His essence
B) A hearing-power (samʿiyya) which is His power over hearing
C) The actual hearing of all sounds
D) A temporal hearing that occurs only when He hears

Key Takeaway
The Karramiyya attempt to preserve God's eternity by distinguishing between eternal powers and temporal acts occurring in His essence, but this still compromises divine immutability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you call God 'All-Hearing' and 'All-Seeing', do you ever think of these as static labels or as active engagements with your life right now? How might your dua change if you truly believed that God's hearing is happening in the present moment, as the Karramiyya claim?
?
The Karramiyya struggled to reconcile God's eternity with His involvement in time. Have you ever felt a tension between God's immutability and the fact that He seems to respond to your prayers at specific moments? What would it cost you to accept that God's actions in time do not compromise His perfection—or that they might, as this lesson suggests?
?
This passage shows a group inventing new categories (powers) to protect God's transcendence. Have you ever constructed mental frameworks to protect your image of God, only to find that they limit Him? Are you willing to let go of your own categories and submit to what revelation actually says, even if it strains your understanding?

The Karramiyya's Internal Disputes and Refutation
Nasafi reports a second Karramiyya subgroup and their disagreement on the permanence of accidents, then refutes both.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second Karramiyya subgroup's view on divine attributes and why Nasafi deems both their positions false.

Core Idea
Nasafi condemns the Karramiyya for either allowing change in God or making Him dependent on originated things.

The Karramiyya were not uniform; some went further by positing distinct powers over attributes themselves. Nasafi refutes this as extreme folly. Moreover, they disagreed about whether these temporal meanings in God could cease. Nasafi declares both opinions false. This lesson examines these internal disputes and the final refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read about the second subgroup's doctrine
Read the passage describing those Karramiyya who affirm distinct powers like knowing-power (ʿālamiyya) as separate from knowledge. They claim God is knowing by this power, not by knowledge itself.
This subgroup makes the attributes dependent on powers that are not themselves attributes.
2
Understand Nasafi's refutation of this view
Nasafi calls this 'the extreme of stupidity and misguidance' because they attribute to God knowledge, power, and life through what is not knowledge, power, or life.
3
Examine the internal disagreement on permanence
The Karramiyya disagreed whether the originated meanings in God's essence can cease to exist. Some allowed it (implying change in God), others denied it (implying that originated things cannot cease, which is also absurd). Nasafi declares both opinions false.
Both positions contradict God's immutability and eternity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
محدثات العالم. وكذا قالوا بحدوث مماسة في ذاته عند مماسته لما يماس من الأجسام، وكذا عند رؤيته شيئا أو سماعه صوتا يحدث فيه تسمع وتبصر المبصرات والمرئيات ويسمونه سميعا في الأزل لا بسمع قائم بذاته بل بسمعيته [بعدد؟] يعنون به قدرته على السمع، وكذا يسمونه بصيرا ببصريته، ثم تبصره وتسمعه محدثان، وكذا كان في الأزل متكلما قائلا لا بقوله وكلامه بل بقائليته ومتكلميته، وهما قدرته على القول والكلام، فأما الكلام فهو يحدث عند تكلمه. وكذا كان في الأزل خالقا بخالقيته ورازقا برازقيته، وهما القدرة على الرزق وعلى الخلق، فأما الخلق والرزق فهما يحدثان في ذاته. هذا هو مذهب جمهورهم وهؤلاء يقولون : إنه عالم بعلمه وقادر بقدرته وحي بحياته، ولا يقولون هو عالم بعالميته وقادر بقادريته وحي بحييته لما أن العالمية والقادرية والحيية قدرة على العلم والقدرة والحياة، وهذا الصفات لا تدخل تحت القدرة، فلا يتصور عالميته ولا قادريته ولا حييته. ومنهم من قال : الخالقية معنى مخصوص به يكون الخالق خالقا وهي غير القدرة، ويقولون : إنه عالم بعالمية وقادر بقادرية وحي بحيية، وهذه المعاني غير القدرة والعلم والحياة. فيجعلونه عالما قادرا حيا بما ليس بعلم ولا قدرة ولا حياة، ولا يجعلونه عالما قادرا حيا بالعلم والقدرة والحياة. وهذا غاية الغباوة والضلالة. ثم بينهم اختلاف في جواز عدم ما حدث في ذاته من المعاني منهم من جوز ذلك، وهذا هو القول بالتغير، ومنهم من لم جوز ذلك وهو القول باستحالة العدم على الحوادث، وكلا القولين باطل.
The originated things of the world. And likewise they said: the occurrence of touching in His essence when He touches what He touches of bodies, and likewise when He sees something or hears a sound, there occurs in Him hearing and seeing of the seen and visible things, and they call Him 'Hearing' in pre-eternity not by a hearing subsisting in His essence but by His hearing-power, intending thereby His power over hearing. And likewise they call Him 'Seeing' by His seeing-power, then His seeing and His hearing are originated. And likewise He was in pre-eternity a Speaker, a Sayer, not by His speech and His word but by His sayer-power and His speaker-power, and they are His power over speech and speaking. As for speech, it occurs when He speaks. And likewise He was in pre-eternity a Creator by His creator-power and a Provider by His provider-power, and they are the power over provision and over creation. As for creation and provision, they occur in His essence. This is the doctrine of the majority of them. And these say: He is knowing by His knowledge, powerful by His power, living by His life, and they do not say He is knowing by His knowing-power, powerful by His power-power, living by His living-power, because knowing-power, power-power, and living-power are power over knowledge, power, and life, and these attributes do not fall under power, so His knowing-power, power-power, and living-power are inconceivable. And among them is one who said: Creator-power is a particular meaning by which the Creator is Creator, and it is other than power. And they say: He is knowing by a knowing-power, powerful by a power-power, living by a living-power, and these meanings are other than power, knowledge, and life. Thus they make Him knowing, powerful, living by what is not knowledge, power, nor life, and they do not make Him knowing, powerful, living by knowledge, power, and life. And this is the extreme of stupidity and misguidance. Then among them there is disagreement concerning the permissibility of the non-existence of what occurred in His essence of the meanings: some permitted that, and this is the doctrine of change; and some did not permit that, and this is the doctrine of the impossibility of non-existence for originated things. And both doctrines are false.
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the Karramiyya doctrine regarding God's attributes. The author first describes their view: they claim that temporal events (ḥawādith) occur in God's essence, such as when He touches bodies, sees something, or hears a sound, then hearing and seeing come to be in Him. They distinguish between eternal attributes of 'hearing-power' (samʿiyya) and 'seeing-power' (baṣariyya) and the actual acts of hearing and seeing which are originated. They similarly hold that God is eternally a Speaker not by an eternal speech but by a speaker-power (qāʾiliyya, mutakallimiyya), while actual speech occurs when He speaks. Likewise, God is eternally a Creator by a creator-power (khāliqiyya) and a Provider by a provider-power (rāziqiyya), while creation and provision occur in His essence. The author then distinguishes two sub-groups among them: the majority affirm that God is knowing by knowledge, powerful by power, and living by life; they reject the notion of 'knowing-power' (ʿālamiyya), 'power-power' (qādariyya), and 'living-power' (ḥayyiyya) because these would be powers over attributes that cannot be subject to power. Another sub-group, however, affirms such powers as distinct entities beyond knowledge, power, and life, attributing to God knowledge and power and life through these instead of through the attributes themselves—a view the author calls extreme stupidity and misguidance. Finally, the author notes that the Karramiyya themselves disagree about the permanence of these originated meanings in God: some allow them to cease (which implies change in God), others deny their cessation (which implies the impossibility of non-existence for originated things). The author declares both positions false.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the Karramiyya internal disagreement is a minor theological nuance without significant consequences.
Correction: Nasafi declares both sides as false because they either imply change in God or posit originated things that cannot cease, both contradicting divine immutability.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what does the second Karramiyya subgroup falsely claim about God's knowledge?
A) God knows by an eternal knowledge that is His attribute.
B) God knows by a knowing-power (ʿālamiyya) which is not knowledge.
C) God knows by both knowledge and a knowing-power.
D) God does not know at all.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi condemns both the second subgroup's theology and the internal dispute over the permanence of accidents, affirming that God is immutable and free from temporal events.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself adding 'conditions' to God's attributes in your mind, like requiring a separate 'power-power' for His power? How does this lesson expose the subtle danger of speculating beyond revelation? Will you surrender your intellect to what God has revealed about Himself, even when it feels incomplete?
?
The Karramiyya tried to protect God from change, but ended up with absurdities. Are there areas in your own belief where you are trying to 'protect' God in ways that actually contradict His self-description? What would it cost you to simply accept His attributes as He describes them, without addition or subtraction?
?
Nasafi calls their view 'extreme stupidity and misguidance'. How do you guard your heart from falling into similar innovation? Do you have the courage to abandon any belief, no matter how logical it seems, once you realize it is not from the Qur'an and Sunnah? Will you commit tonight to studying God's names and attributes only from the revealed sources?

The Principle of Devoidness and Its Application to God
Author establishes a key premise and applies it to refute the Karramiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why something that is inherently devoid of temporal events cannot become a locus for them, and how this principle refutes the claim that God's essence contains temporal takwin.

Core Idea
What is free from temporals by its nature can never become their locus.

The argument against the temporality of takwin begins with a fundamental principle: anything that is essentially devoid of temporal events is forever immune to them. The author first establishes this principle and then applies it directly to God's essence, demonstrating the impossibility of takwin being a temporal accident within Him.

Guided Path
1
Read the initial premise
Read the first part where the author states that something devoid of temporal events cannot have them befall it. Note the reasoning: it is devoid by its own essence.
The term 'devoid' here means free from temporal events by nature.
2
Understand the two scenarios
The author considers two possibilities: either the state of being devoid is by essence (then it is impossible for it to be lost) or by a meaning (then that meaning either remains or ceases).
Each scenario leads to a contradiction or a sign of temporality.
3
See the dilemma unfold
If the meaning remains, there is a combination of attributes (devoidness and event) which is contradictory. If it ceases, the subject was not eternal, because a true eternal cannot lose a meaning.
This shows that the supposed subject cannot be eternal if it acquires temporals.
4
Connect to the refutation
The author applies this to God: if God were to have temporal takwin, He would not be free of temporals, which is a sign of createdness. Thus, the Karramiyya claim is false.
This argument also proves the temporality of the world and refutes the concept of hyle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللمتكلمين كلام كثير في إبطال كونه خالقا بالخالقية ومريدا بالمريدية وغير ذلك أعرضنا مخافة التطويل واشتغلنا بإبطال كون التكوين حادثا في ذاته وكونه محلا للحوادث فنقول : الرد على كلام الكرامية إنا قد بينا قبل هذا أن ما كان متعريا عن الحوادث يستحيل اعتراء الحوادث عليه، لأنه كان متعريا لذاته فيستحيل بطلان التعري والذات باق ويستحيل حدوث الحوادث مع وجود التعري، لما في الاتصاف بالتعري عن الحوادث وبقيام الحوادث به من المضادة، فلو كان متعريا لمعنى إن لم ينعدم ذلك المعنى ففيه اجتماع الوصفين أيضا، وإن انعدم علم أنه لم يكن قديما لاستحالة القدم عليه، وإذا لم يكن قديما والذات لا تخلو عنه وعن هذه الحوادث، فلم يخل عن جنس الحوادث وهذا هو أمارة الحدث. وبهذا عرفنا حدوث العالم وبطلان قول أصحاب الهيولى ولو جاز هذا في الصانع مع قدمه لجاز في الهيولى وفي جميع أجسام العالم والقول بقدم العالم باطل، فما كان يوجبها ويساويه في دليل البطلان كان باطلا. يحققه أن المعنى الحادث في ذاته إما أن يكون جائز العدم أو يكون ممتنع العدم، فإن كان جائز العدم أدى ذلك إلى القول بتعاقب الحوادث عليه وهو من أمارات الحدث، وإن كان ممتنع العدم فهو أزلي، لأنه إذا كان ممتنع العدم كان واجب الوجود، وما كان واجب الوجود فهو أزلي على ما مر قبل هذا، وفيه صحة قولنا ومناقضة قوله حيث جعل واجب الوجود حادثا، ولأن استحالة قبوله الحادث في الأزل إما أن كان لذاته وذاته موجود، وإما أن كان لمعنى والعدم على ذلك المعنى ممتنع فاستحال الآن أيضا قبوله للحوادث. وظهر بهذا بطلان حدوث التكوين في ذاته تعالى، وجاء من هذا أن الأقسام التي ينقسم إليها التكوين لو كان حادثا كلها ممتنعة فامتنع القول بحدوثه من أن إثبات حدوثه إثبات أمر ممتنع، وإثبات الممتنع محال. وإذا بطلت هذه الوجوه تعين القول بقدمه.
And the mutakallimun have much speech in nullifying that He is Creator by the attribute of creator-ness and Willer by the attribute of willer-ness and other than that. We turned away for fear of length and occupied ourselves with nullifying that takwin (bringing into existence) is temporal in His essence and that He is a locus for temporal events. So we say: Refutation of the statement of the Karramiyya: We have explained before this that that which is devoid of temporal events, it is impossible for temporal events to befall it, because it was devoid by its own essence, so the invalidation of the state of being devoid is impossible while the essence remains, and the occurrence of temporal events is impossible with the existence of the state of being devoid, due to the contradiction between being qualified with devoidness of temporal events and the subsistence of temporal events in it. So if it were devoid by a meaning, if that meaning does not cease, then there is still the combination of the two attributes; and if it ceases, then it is known that it was not eternal because of the impossibility of eternality upon it. And if it is not eternal, and the essence is not free of it and of these temporal events, then it is not free of the genus of temporal events, and this is the sign of temporal origination. And by this we know the temporal origination of the world and the invalidity of the statement of the followers of hyle. And if this were permissible in the case of the Maker with His eternality, it would be permissible in the case of hyle and all bodies of the world, and the statement that the world is eternal is false. So whatever necessitates them and is equal to it in the proof of invalidity is false. He verifies it: the temporal meaning in His essence is either possible of non-existence or impossible of non-existence. If it is possible of non-existence, that leads to the statement of succession of temporal events upon it, and that is from the signs of temporal origination. And if it is impossible of non-existence, then it is eternal, because if it is impossible of non-existence, it is necessary of existence, and whatever is necessary of existence is eternal as has passed before this. And in this is the correctness of our statement and the contradiction of his statement where he made the Necessary of Existence temporal. And because the impossibility of its acceptance of the temporal in pre-eternality: either it was by its own essence while its essence exists, or it was by a meaning, and non-existence of that meaning is impossible, so it is also impossible now for it to accept temporal events. And by this the invalidity of the temporality of takwin in His exalted essence became clear, and it follows from this that the categories into which takwin would be divided if it were temporal are all impossible, so the statement of its temporality is impossible, because affirming its temporality is affirming an impossible matter, and affirming the impossible is absurd. And when these aspects are invalidated, the statement of its eternality is determined.
Source pages p. 550

Commentary
This passage is a proof refuting the Karramiyya claim that takwin is a temporal accident in God's essence. The author begins by stating his intention to nullify the idea that takwin is temporal and that God is a locus for accidents. He then presents a structured argument. First, he reiterates an earlier premise: something that is devoid of temporal events cannot have temporal events befall it because freedom from temporals is essential to it. If it were free by virtue of a meaning, either that meaning remains (contradictorily combining freedom and the event) or ceases (showing non-eternality). This is then applied to God: if He were devoid of temporals but then acquired them, He would not be eternal. Consequently, whatever becomes subject to successive temporals is temporally originated. This argument is then used to prove the temporality of the world and refute the concept of hyle. Next, the author analyzes a temporal meaning in God's essence: it is either possible of non-existence (leading to succession, a sign of temporality) or impossible of non-existence (making it eternal and necessary). The latter contradicts the opponent's position of making the Necessary Existent temporal. Finally, he concludes that takwin must be eternal, as its temporal existence would involve impossible consequences.

الحوادث
التعري
القدم
الحدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God can be a locus for temporal accidents like takwin.
Correction: The author argues that God is essentially devoid of temporals; therefore, it is impossible for Him to become their locus.

Checkpoint
According to the author, if something is devoid of temporal events by a meaning, and that meaning ceases, what does this indicate?
A) The entity remains eternal.
B) The entity was not eternal.
C) The meaning was temporary.
D) The entity becomes free of temporals.

Key Takeaway
The principle that what is essentially devoid of temporals cannot receive them refutes the Karramiyya position that takwin is a temporal accident in God's essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel that God is distant or silent, do you unconsciously assume He has changed, or do you anchor your faith in His timeless perfection, as this lesson teaches?
?
If God were subject to the same temporal fluctuations as your own emotions, would you still be able to trust Him absolutely? How does this lesson's truth reshape your reliance on Him?
?
The argument shows that nothing can enter God's essence—no accident, no change. Does your worship reflect awe of a God who is utterly transcendent, or have you reduced Him to a being who responds to you like a mutable creature?

The Dilemma of Temporal Meaning: Takwin Must Be Eternal
Author presents a dilemma and concludes that takwin must be eternal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why any temporal meaning in God's essence leads to either impossible succession or eternal necessity, thus proving takwin cannot be temporal.

Core Idea
A temporal meaning in God is either possible of non-existence (leading to succession) or impossible (making it eternal).

The author sharpens the argument by examining the nature of the supposed temporal meaning in God's essence. He poses a clear dilemma: either the meaning can cease to exist, leading to a succession of events (a sign of temporality), or it cannot cease, implying it is eternal and necessary. Both options contradict the opponent's claim that takwin is a temporal accident.

Guided Path
1
Read the dilemma
Read the passage starting from 'He verifies it'. The author presents two possibilities for a temporal meaning in God's essence: it is either possible of non-existence or impossible of non-existence.
These two options are exhaustive for any contingent accident.
2
Analyze the first branch
If the meaning is possible of non-existence (i.e., it can cease), then it will be followed by another meaning, leading to a succession of temporals. This is a sign of createdness.
Succession of accidents is a mark of contingency.
3
Analyze the second branch
If the meaning is impossible of non-existence, then it must be necessary of existence, and therefore eternal. This contradicts the opponent's claim that it is temporal.
Something necessary of existence cannot be temporal.
4
Understand the final conclusion
Both branches lead to an impossibility for the opponent. The author also argues that the impossibility of temporals in pre-eternality continues now, and that all categories of temporal takwin are impossible, so takwin must be eternal.
This seals the refutation.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of a temporal meaning in God's essence proves that takwin must be eternal, not a temporal accident.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God 'creating' the universe, do you subconsciously imagine a moment in time when He acted? How does the argument that takwin is eternal challenge that imagination, and what is the first step you can take today to think of creation as an eternal relation rather than a past event?
?
If affirming a temporal meaning in God leads to absurdities, examine your own heart: are you holding onto any thought about God that, if followed to its logical conclusion, would contradict His perfection? Are you willing to abandon that thought for tawheed?
?
The author says that if takwin were temporal, it would be impossible to affirm. Consider one specific blessing in your life right now. Do you see it as the result of a one-time act of creation, or as continuously sustained by God's eternal attribute of takwin? How can you train your soul to feel this continuous dependence?

Objection to the Eternality of Takwin
Objection to takwin's eternality with three arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three arguments raised by those who claim takwin is temporal and why they consider the claim of its eternality impossible.

Core Idea
The objection to takwin's eternality rests on tradition, language, and logic — none of which, the objector argues, can accommodate an eternal creation.

This passage presents a compound objection from proponents of takwin's temporality. They argue that the claim of takwin's eternality is not just unlikely but impossible, citing three distinct reasons: lack of precedent among the Salaf, linguistic implications, and logical consequences. The objection challenges the Maturidi position that takwin is an eternal attribute distinct from creation. Let's examine the objection's structure and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and identify its structure
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice it begins by framing the objection and then presents three arguments. Identify the three arguments in the text.
The passage ends abruptly with 'فإن', indicating the answer continues in the next lesson.
2
Understand the first argument: innovation and lack of Salafi support
The first argument states that the claim of takwin's eternality is an innovation (قول مستحدث) with no precedent among the Salaf. This argument relies on authority and tradition.
3
Understand the second argument: linguistic consistency
The second argument draws an analogy with other attributes: if creation (khalq) were eternal, it would be permissible to say 'He created in pre-eternity' just as we say 'He knows' and 'He is able'. This challenges the linguistic consistency of the claim.
4
Understand the third argument: logical implication of co-eternal creation
The third argument uses the relationship between an attribute and its effect. If takwin is eternal, then the world must be co-eternal because takwin necessarily relates to an existent (mukawwan), just as knowledge relates to an eternal known. This would lead to the belief in the world's eternality.
The objector concludes that this consequence is unacceptable, hence takwin cannot be eternal.

And if the world were composed and created in pre-eternity, then the statement of the world's eternality would be established, because that which is composed and created will only be existent. As for the non-existent, it is neither composed nor created, unlike the empowered and the known, for

Commentary
This passage presents an objection by those who claim takwin is temporal. The objector argues that the determination of takwin's eternality is not necessary, as other possibilities are equally impossible. Three arguments are given: 1) The claim of eternal takwin is an innovation without Salafi precedent. 2) If creation were an eternal attribute, one could say 'He created in pre-eternity' just as one says 'He knows' and 'He is able,' implying a co-eternal creation. 3) If takwin were eternal, the world would be co-eternal because the relation of takwin to its effect is like the relation of knowledge to the known; since the cause is eternal, the effect would be eternal. The Eternity of Takwin: Logical Proof from Impossibility
Imam al-Nasafi proves the eternity of takwin through impossibility of origination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument for the eternity of the divine attribute of takwin (creation) based on the impossibility of its temporal origination.

Core Idea
Takwin cannot be temporal because that would imply an impossibility.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents a sophisticated argument to demonstrate that takwin (the attribute of bringing things into existence) must be eternal (qadim) and cannot have originated in time (hadith). He begins by establishing that God, as the Necessary Being, cannot become a locus for temporal occurrences. Then he shows that if takwin were temporal, its conceptual divisions would be impossible, leading to a contradiction. The argument ultimately forces the conclusion of eternity.

Guided Path
1
Understand the refutation of making God temporal
The author first refutes the opponent's claim that the Necessary Being could be temporal. He argues that the impossibility of accepting temporal things in pre-eternity is either due to God's essence or due to a meaning, and in both cases it persists, so now also acceptance is impossible.
This shows that temporal attributes cannot arise in God.
2
See how takwin's temporal origination is invalidated
From the above, it follows that takwin itself cannot be temporal because that would require God to accept a temporal quality, which is impossible.
Takwin is an attribute, so its occurrence would be a temporal event in God.
3
Follow the reductio ad absurdum on takwin's divisions
The author then argues that if takwin were temporal, all its possible divisions (like bringing things forth at different times) would be impossible, leading to an absurdity. Therefore, affirming its temporal origination is affirming an impossibility, which is absurd, so the only option is eternity.
This second argument reinforces the first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولنا ومناقضة قوله حيث جعل واجب الوجود حادثا، ولأن استحالة قبوله الحادث في الأزل إما أن كان لذاته وذاته موجود، وإما أن كان لمعنى والعدم على ذلك المعنى ممتنع فاستحال الآن أيضا قبوله للحوادث. وظهر بهذا بطلان حدوث التكوين في ذاته تعالى، وجاء من هذا أن الأقسام التي ينقسم إليها التكوين لو كان حادثا كلها ممتنعة فامتنع القول بحدوثه من أن إثبات حدوثه إثبات أمر ممتنع، وإثبات الممتنع محال. وإذا بطلت هذه الوجوه تعين القول بقدمه.
Our statement: and a refutation of his statement where he made the Necessary Being temporal. And because the impossibility of its accepting the temporal in pre-eternity is either due to its essence and its essence exists, or due to a meaning and non-existence of that meaning is impossible, so now also its acceptance of temporal things is impossible. And by this the invalidity of the temporal origination of takwin (creative attribute) in His essence, exalted is He, became clear. And from this it follows that the divisions into which takwin would be divided, if it were temporal, are all impossible, so the statement of its temporal origination is impossible, because affirming its temporal origination is affirming an impossible matter, and affirming the impossible is absurd. And when these aspects are invalidated, the statement of its eternity is determined.
Source pages p. 551

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for the eternity (qidam) of takwin (the attribute of creation) and the impossibility of its temporal origination (huduth). The argument begins by refuting an opponent who makes the Necessary Being (wajib al-wujud) temporal. The author argues that the impossibility of accepting temporal things in pre-eternity (al-azal) is either due to God's essence (dhat) or due to some meaning. In either case, that impossibility persists, so accepting temporal things is still impossible. Consequently, the temporal origination of takwin in God's essence is invalid. Then he argues that if takwin were temporal, all its divisions would be impossible, which is absurd. Therefore, affirming its temporal origination is affirming an impossibility, which is impossible. Hence, since all these proofs fail, the only valid position is that takwin is eternal (qadim).

Key Terms
التكوين (takwin)
الحدوث (huduth)
القدم (qidam)
واجب الوجود (wajib al-wujud)
الأزل (al-azal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof relies on an a priori claim rather than logical necessity from the impossibility of attributes in the Necessary Being.
Correction: The argument is based on the logical impossibility of the Necessary Being receiving temporal attributes, which is derived from the nature of necessity itself, not an arbitrary assumption.

Checkpoint

A) Its divisions become possible.
B) It leads to affirming an impossibility.
C) It becomes necessary for the world to be eternal.
D) It necessitates God's inability.

Key Takeaway
Takwin, the attribute of creation, must be eternal because its temporal origination would lead to logical impossibilities.

Does your worship reflect a trust in a God whose creative power is always present, or do you act as if He is only powerful when you see results? What would change if you truly believed takwin is eternal and always active?

The Argument from Divine Praise for the Eternity of Takwin
al-Nasafi refutes objections by proving takwin's eternity through divine praise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Nasafi uses Allah's self-praise as al-Khaliq to prove that takwin is eternal, and why temporal attributes would imply defect.

Core Idea
Divine self-praise demands eternal attributes, for temporality implies defect.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi responds to those who claim takwin is temporal. Rather than simply asserting possibility, he argues that takwin must be eternal because Allah has praised Himself as 'the Creator' in the Quran. If this attribute were temporal, Allah would have been imperfect before its existence, which is impossible. This lesson unpacks that decisive argument.

Guided Path
1
Review the objections against takwin's eternity
Read the initial objections: that the claim is novel, that an eternal attribute would imply an eternal product, and that takwin without a product implies incapability. These set up the problem.
The opponents demand proof of possibility first.
2
Understand the counter-argument from divine praise
Focus on the answer: al-Nasafi begins by acknowledging the requirement to prove possibility, but then shifts to proving obligation (wajib). The key move is to cite Qur'anic verses where Allah praises Himself as Creator, then argue that if this attribute were temporal, the praise would be absent before its existence, implying defect. Defect is a sign of temporality.
Notice the logical chain: praise → perfection → no defect → eternity.
3
Examine the analogy between essence and attributes
The passage extends the argument: just as defect in essence (e.g., being created) indicates temporality, so defect in attributes indicates temporality. Since Allah's essence has no defect, His attributes cannot have defect either. Thus takwin must be eternal.
This reinforces the conclusion by parity of reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبه أخرى للقائلين بحدوث التكوين فإن قيل : إنما تتعين بعض الوجوه عند ثبوت امتناع ما وراءه، أن لو ثبت أن هذا الوجه ممكن فأما عند ثبوت امتناعه، فلا يتعين لمساواة سائر الوجوه الممتنعة إياه. فلم قلتم : إن القول بقدم التكوين ممكن وليس بممتنع، بل هو ممتنع لما أنه قول مستحدث لا قائل به من السلف، ولأن الخلق لو كان صفة له أزلية لصح أن يقال : خلق في الأزل، كما يصح أن يقال : علم وقدر، ولأنه لو كان في الأزل موجودا لكان العالم مكونا مخلوقا لأن سبيل الخلق أن يتعلق بالمخلوق، وسبيل التكوين أن يتعلق بالمكون، كما أن العلم لما كان يتعلق بالمعلوم وكذا القدرة بالمقدور وهما كانا أزليين صح المعلوم والمقدور في الأزل، ولو كان العالم مكونا مخلوقا في الأزل لثبت القول بقدم العالم، لأن المكون المخلوق لن يكون إلا الموجود، فأما المعدوم فلا يكون مكونا ولا مخلوقا بخلاف المقدور والمعلوم فإن المعدوم يوصف بذلك، فعلى هذا كان القول بقدم التكوين قولا بقدم العالم الذي ثبت حدوثه بالدلائل الضرورية، ولأن القول بوجود التكوين ولا مكون إثبات العجز، وهو محال على الله تعالى. فيجاب عن هذا الكلام بأن يقال : نعم الأمر كما زعمتم أن تعيين وجه من الوجوه لا يمكن عند امتناع غيره من الوجوه إلا بعد إثبات إمكانه، وأنصفتم حيث طالبتمونا بإثبات الإمكان، ونحن لا نرضى بذلك بل نزيد عليه ونقول: إن القول بقدمه واجب، وذلك لأن الله تعالى تمدح بقوله تعالى: ﴿ هُوَ اللهُ الْخَلِقُ الْبَارِئُ الْمُصَوِّرُ ﴾ كما تمدح بقوله: ﴿ هُوَ اللهُ الَّذِى لا إله إلا هو الملك القدوس السلامُ الْمُؤْمِنُ الْمُهَيْمِنُ الْعَزِيزُ الْجَبَّارُ الْمُتَكَبَرُ ﴾ . ثم زوال ما به التمدح يوجب نقصا، إذ لا شك أن الذات عند استحقاق المدح تكون أكمل منه عند انعدام استحقاقه والنقص من أمارات الحدث، ولهذا لا يجوز عليه شيء من صفات النقص إذ النقص من حيث الذات كما هو دليل الحدوث، فكذا النقص من حيث الصفات إذ ذات ما كما لا تقتضي نقصه من حيث الذات لا يقتضي نقصه من حيث الصفات، وكما أن نقصه من حيث الذات يثبت بإثبات غيره فيه ليدل على كونه تحت قدرة الغير ويستدل بنقصه على كمال من هو قادر عليه، فكذا في النقص الثابت من حيث الصفات.
Further objections for those who say takwin is temporal: Then it is said: A particular aspect is determined only when the impossibility of what is beyond it is established, if it is established that this aspect is possible. But when its impossibility is established, it is not determined because it equals the other impossible aspects. So why do you say that the statement of the eternity of takwin is possible and not impossible? Rather it is impossible because it is a novel statement not held by any of the predecessors, and because if creation were an eternal attribute of Him, it would be correct to say: He created in pre-eternity, just as it is correct to say: He knew and was powerful. And because if it existed in pre-eternity, the world would be created and made, because the way of creation is that it is attached to the created thing, and the way of takwin is that it is attached to the thing made. Just as knowledge is attached to the known and power to the thing capable, and both were eternal, so the known and the thing capable existed in pre-eternity. And if the world were made and created in pre-eternity, the statement of the eternity of the world would be established. For the made and created thing can only be existent. As for the non-existent, it is not made nor created, unlike the thing capable and the known, for the non-existent is described by those. Hence, on this, the statement of the eternity of takwin is a statement of the eternity of the world, whose temporality is established by necessary proofs. And because the statement of the existence of takwin with no thing made is an affirmation of incapability, which is impossible for Allah Almighty. The answer to this speech is to say: Yes, the matter is as you claimed, that the determination of an aspect is not possible when others are impossible except after proving its possibility, and you have been fair in requiring us to prove possibility. But we are not content with that; rather we add to it and say: The statement of its eternity is obligatory. That is because Allah Almighty praised Himself by His saying: 'He is Allah, the Creator, the Originator, the Formulator' (59:24), just as He praised Himself by His saying: 'He is Allah, other than whom there is no deity, the Sovereign, the Holy, the Safety, the Guardian, the Exalted in Might, the Compeller, the Superior' (59:23). Then the removal of that by which praise is given entails defect. For there is no doubt that the essence when deserving praise is more perfect than when its desert is absent, and defect is a sign of temporality. Therefore none of the attributes of defect are permissible for Him. For defect in terms of essence, just as it is proof of temporality, so too defect in terms of attributes, since an essence which does not imply its own defect in terms of essence does not imply its defect in terms of attributes. And just as His defect in terms of essence is established by the affirmation of another in it to indicate that it is under the power of another, and one infers from its defect the perfection of the one who is able over it, so too regarding the defect established in terms of attributes.
Source pages p. 551

Commentary
This passage presents a series of objections against the eternity of takwin followed by a detailed refutation. The objections (shubah) include: (1) that the claim of eternity is a novel statement not held by predecessors; (2) if creation were eternal, one could say 'He created in pre-eternity' like 'He knew'; (3) if takwin existed in pre-eternity, the world would be eternal since the product of creation (mukawwan) must exist; (4) affirming takwin without a product implies incapability. The answer begins by acknowledging the opponent's condition about proving possibility but argues that the statement of eternity is actually obligatory (wajib). The proof is based on divine praise (tamadhuh): Allah praised Himself as al-Khaliq (the Creator) in the Quran. If this attribute were temporal (hadith), then before its existence Allah would not have deserved that praise, implying a defect (naqs). Defect is a sign of temporality (hadath). Thus, since defect is impossible for Allah, takwin must be eternal. The argument extends to show that defect in attributes is analogous to defect in essence—both indicate dependence on another and thus temporality.

Key Terms
التكوين (takwin)
القدم (qidam)
التمددح (tamadhuh)
الخلق (khalq)
النقص (naqs)
الحدث (hadath)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument from divine praise is circular because it assumes the attribute is eternal to justify its presence in the Quran.
Correction: The argument is not circular; it uses the Qur'anic description as a given fact of revelation, then deduces the attribute's eternity based on the impossibility of temporal defect. The premise is Allah's self-praise, not the eternality itself.

Checkpoint
What is the main basis for the answer's proof that takwin must be eternal?
A) The consensus of the Salaf.
B) The logical impossibility of a temporal creator.
C) Allah's self-praise as al-Khaliq in the Quran.
D) The necessity of a product for any action.

Key Takeaway
Takwin is eternal because Allah's self-praise as Creator would be meaningless if it were temporal, as that would imply a defect unbecoming of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah’s attribute of creation is eternal, that means He has always been creating. Do you truly live with the awareness that at every moment your existence is being brought about by Him, or do you subconsciously act as if you have an independent existence? How would your daily choices change if you internalized this constant dependence?
?
The argument equates a temporary attribute with a defect. Think about your own character—where do you see a ‘temporary’ virtue that you only practice occasionally? Doesn't that inconsistency reveal something about your own limitations? How can you begin to make your good qualities more constant, reflecting the divine attribute you seek to imitate?
?
Al-Nasafi insists that divine praise is only meaningful if the attribute praised is eternal. When you praise Allah as ‘the Creator’, do you ever catch yourself treating it as a past event (He created once, then stopped)? What would it mean for your worship to truly believe that His creative act is ongoing, and how would that transform your prayer today?

The Eternal Praise Argument for Takwin
Nasafi presents the argument from divine self-praise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses God's self-praise as al-Khaliq, al-Bari', and al-Musawwir to prove that takwin must be eternal.

Core Idea
God's eternal praise requires eternal attributes.

Nasafi counters the objection that eternal takwin implies an eternal world by starting with a key theological principle: God praises Himself with specific names in the Quran. If these names were not eternally true, God would have acquired perfection later, implying deficiency—a sign of temporality. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on divine praise
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice how Nasafi first acknowledges the opponent's point before moving to his own argument.
The opponent's premise is that specifying a mode requires establishing possibility.
2
Identify the Quranic proof
Nasafi cites Quran 59:24 and 59:23. Understand that God praises Himself with these names, and the praise must be eternal.
3
Trace the implication of deficiency
If the attributes were not eternal, God would have been deficient before creation. Deficiency is a sign of temporality, which is impossible for God.
This leads to the absurdity that God would be temporal in pre-eternity.
4
Connect to takwin
Realize that takwin is the attribute that grounds these names. If takwin is not eternal, the names are not eternal, leading to the contradiction above.

المعدوم يوصف بذلك، فعلى هذا كان القول بقدم التكوين قولا بقدم العالم الذي ثبت حدوثه بالدلائل الضرورية، ولأن القول بوجود التكوين ولا مكون إثبات العجز، وهو محال على الله تعالى. فيجاب عن هذا الكلام بأن يقال : نعم الأمر كما زعمتم أن تعيين وجه من الوجوه لا يمكن عند امتناع غيره من الوجوه إلا بعد إثبات إمكانه، وأنصفتم حيث طالبتمونا بإثبات الأماكن، ونحن لا نرضى بذلك بل نزيد عليه ونقول: إن القول بقدمه واجب، وذلك لأن الله تعالى تمدح بقوله تعالى: ﴿ هُوَ اللهُ الْخَلِقُ الْبَارِئُ الْمُصَوِّرُ ﴾ كما تمدح بقوله: ﴿ هُوَ اللهُ الَّذِى لا إله إلا هو الملك القدوس السلامُ الْمُؤْمِنُ الْمُهَيْمِنُ الْعَزِيزُ الْجَبَّارُ الْمُتَكَبَرُ ﴾ . ثم زوال ما به التمدح يوجب نقصا، إذ لا شك أن الذات عند استحقاق المدح تكون أكمل منه عند انعدام استحقاقه والنقص من أمارات الحدث، ولهذا لا يجوز عليه شيء من صفات النقص من حيث الذات كما هو دليل الحدوث، فكذا النقص من حيث الصفات إذ ذات ما كما لا تقتضي نقصه من حيث الذات لا يقتضي نقصه من حيث الصفات، وكما أن نقصه من حيث الذات يثبت بإثبات غيره فيه ليدل على كونه تحت قدرة الغير ويستدل بنقصه على كمال من هو قادر عليه، فكذا في النقص الثابت من حيث الصفات، فمن لم يجعله خالقا بارئا مصورا في الأزل، فقد زعم أن الله تعالى في الأزل كان أنقص منه الآن، والنقص من أمارات الحدث، فإذا ثبت في القدم دليل حدوث الله تعالى جل ربنا عن ذلك، فكان الله تعالى - على زعم هذا القائل - في الأزل محدثا، وكون الأزلي محدثا محال . وكون ذات واحد محدثا قديما ممتنع - ولأنه لو صار خالق يخلق حادث لصار بموجود المخلوقات ممدوحا فحصل له التمدح بغيره لا بنفسه، فكان محتاجا إلى وجود ذلك الغير ليدفع به نقصه، إذ الحاجة ليست إلا نقصا يرتفع بالمطلوب وينجبر به ولأنه لو كان كذلك لصار بفعله جالبا إلى نفسه نفعا مكتسبا ما يستفيد به مدحا ورفعة وكمال درجة وجلال قدر، وهذا كله من أمارات الحاجة ودلائل النقص وسمات الحدوث، وكل محدث مخلوق لا خالق، فإذا كان الخالق عندهم مخلوقا، ولأنه تعالى لو لم يكن خالقا ثم صار خالقا وقد مر أن استحقاقه الوصف إما أن يكون بصفة قائمة بالذات أو بصفة راجعة إلى الذات، وصفة الخلق ليست براجعة إلى ذاته بل هي وراء ذاته بالإجماع، فلو لم تكن قائمة بالذات لم يكن مستحقا اسم الخالق بها على ما بينا، ثم إذا صار خالقا صار لقيامه به فيصير متغيرا عند صيرورته خالقا إذ الذات بحدوث صفة فيه لم تكن ثابتة يتغير عما كان عليه، والتغير من أمارات الحدوث، فإذا يصير مخلوقا عند صيرورته خالقا ، وصار من يعبد الخالق عابد المخلوق، وهذا كله محال. والذي يحققه أن من يجوز عليه الفعل لا ينتفي عنه الفعل إلا عن عجز،
The non-existent is described by that, so on this basis, the statement that takwin (bringing into existence) is eternal is a statement that the world is eternal, while its temporality has been established by necessary proofs. And because the statement of the existence of takwin without a thing brought into existence is an affirmation of incapability, and that is impossible for Allah the Exalted. So this speech is answered by saying: Yes, the matter is as you claimed that specifying one face among faces is not possible when its other faces are impossible except after establishing its possibility, and you were fair when you demanded from us the establishment of the places. But we are not satisfied with that; rather we add to it and say: Indeed, the statement of its eternity is obligatory, and that is because Allah the Exalted praised Himself by His saying: 'He is Allah, the Creator, the Maker, the Fashioner' just as He praised Himself by His saying: 'He is Allah, other than whom there is no deity, the King, the Holy, the Peace, the Guardian, the Mighty, the Compeller, the Superior.' Then the removal of that by which praise is earned necessitates deficiency, since there is no doubt that the essence when deserving praise is more perfect than it when it lacks that deserving. And deficiency is among the signs of temporality, and for this reason nothing of the attributes of deficiency is permissible for Him. In terms of essence, just as it is a proof of temporality, so too deficiency in terms of attributes, for a certain essence just as it does not necessitate its deficiency in terms of essence, it does not necessitate its deficiency in terms of attributes. And just as His deficiency in terms of essence is established by establishing something else in it to indicate that it is under the power of another, and one infers from its deficiency the perfection of the one who is capable over it, so too in the deficiency established in terms of attributes. So whoever does not make Him a Creator, a Maker, a Fashioner in pre-eternity, has claimed that Allah the Exalted in pre-eternity was more deficient than He is now, and deficiency is among the signs of temporality. So if in pre-eternity there is established a proof of the temporality of Allah the Exalted—glory be to our Lord above that—then Allah the Exalted, according to this speaker, would be in pre-eternity temporally originated, and the pre-eternal being temporally originated is impossible. And it is impossible for one essence to be both temporally originated and eternal. And because if He were to become a Creator creating a temporal thing, He would become praised by the existence of created things, so He would obtain praise by other than Himself, so He would be in need of the existence of that other to repel His deficiency. For need is nothing but a deficiency that is removed by the desired thing and compensated by it. And because if it were so, He would become by His action drawing benefit to Himself, acquiring that by which He obtains praise and elevation and perfection of degree and majesty of status. All of this is among the signs of need, proofs of deficiency, and marks of temporality. And every temporally originated thing is created, not a creator. So if the Creator according to them is created. And because if He the Exalted were not a Creator then became a Creator, and it has passed that His deserving of the description is either by an attribute subsisting in the essence or by an attribute returning to the essence, and the attribute of creation does not return to His essence but is beyond His essence by consensus. So if it were not subsisting in the essence, He would not deserve the name Creator by it as we have explained. Then when He becomes a Creator, He becomes so by its subsisting in Him, so He becomes changed at the time of His becoming a Creator, for the essence, by the temporality of an attribute in it, is not stable; it changes from what it was. And change is among the signs of temporality. So He becomes created at the time of His becoming a Creator, and the worshipper of the Creator becomes a worshipper of a created thing. All of this is impossible. And what verifies it is that one upon whom action is permissible, action is not absent from him except due to incapacity.
Source pages p. 552

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the argument that affirming the eternity of the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence) necessarily implies the eternity of the world. The author, Nasafi, responds by first acknowledging the opponent's premise that specifying a particular mode requires establishing its possibility, but then he goes further to assert that the eternity of takwin is obligatory. He bases this on the fact that God praises Himself with names like al-Khaliq (the Creator), al-Bari' (the Maker), and al-Musawwir (the Fashioner) in the Quran. If these attributes were not eternal, then God would have acquired perfection later, implying deficiency in pre-eternity. Deficiency is a sign of temporality (huduth), so attributing deficiency to God would entail that God Himself is temporal, which is impossible. Nasafi then argues that if God became a Creator only at the time of creation, His praise would depend on something other than Himself, indicating need and deficiency. Need is also a mark of temporality. Moreover, if the attribute of creation is not subsisting in God's essence, He would not deserve the name 'Creator' eternally; but if it arises later, it would imply change in God, which is also a sign of temporality. The conclusion is that denying the eternity of takwin leads to absurdities such as God being temporal, dependent, and even created, which are all impossible. The final sentence encapsulates the core point: if action is possible for God, it cannot be absent except due to incapacity; since God is not incapable, takwin must be eternal.

Key Terms
تكوين (takwin)
قدم (qidam)
مدح (madh)
نقص (naqs)
خالق (Khaliq)
بارئ (Bari')
مصور (Musawwir)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That denying the eternity of takwin does not affect God's perfection because God only becomes Creator at the moment of creation.
Correction: Nasafi shows that if takwin is not eternal, then God's praise as al-Khaliq would be acquired later, implying prior deficiency, which is a sign of temporality and impossible for God.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what does God's self-praise as al-Khaliq, al-Bari', and al-Musawwir prove about takwin?
A) Takwin is a temporal attribute
B) Takwin must be eternal
C) Takwin is identical to the created world
D) Takwin is only applicable after creation

Key Takeaway
God's eternal self-praise as Creator proves that takwin is an eternal attribute, not a temporal act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read God's names 'al-Khaliq, al-Bari', al-Musawwir', do you truly believe He possessed these attributes from eternity, or have you ever subconsciously assumed He 'became' Creator only when He created? How might this subconscious assumption affect your understanding of God's perfection and your dependence on Him?
?
If you deny that takwin is eternal, then according to Nasafi, you are saying God was less perfect before creation. Is your heart comfortable with the idea that God could be described as 'not yet Creator' in pre-eternity? How does that challenge your view of His absolute perfection?
?
God praises Himself as Creator from pre-eternity. How does this reality confront your tendency to think of God's actions as separate from His essence? Are you living as if your existence is merely a product of a temporal act, or as a continuous manifestation of His eternal attribute of creation? Commit to reflecting on your absolute dependence on His eternal creating power today.

Refuting Need and Change in Takwin
Nasafi presents arguments from need and change against the temporality of takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's arguments that if takwin were not eternal, God would be dependent on creation and subject to change, both of which are impossible for God.

Core Idea
Non-eternal takwin implies need and change in God.

Nasafi continues his refutation by addressing two further absurdities: if God only becomes a Creator at the moment of creation, He would depend on creation for perfection and would undergo change. Both need and change are marks of temporality, which cannot be attributed to God. This lesson examines these arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the arguments from need and change
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Look for the two main sub-arguments: one about need (haja) and one about change (taghayyur).
Nasafi uses logical consequences to show impossibility.
2
Understand the need argument
If God becomes Creator later, He would gain praise from the existence of creatures. That means His perfection depends on something other than Himself, which is need (deficiency).
Need is a sign of temporality.
3
Understand the change argument
If the attribute of creation arises later in God, His essence changes. Change is also a sign of temporality.
This would make the Creator created, which is absurd.
4
Connect to takwin's eternity
Both arguments lead to the conclusion that denying the eternity of takwin forces absurdities, so takwin must be eternal.

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the argument that affirming the eternity of the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence) necessarily implies the eternity of the world. The author, Nasafi, responds by first acknowledging the opponent's premise that specifying a particular mode requires establishing its possibility, but then he goes further to assert that the eternity of takwin is obligatory. He bases this on the fact that God praises Himself with names like al-Khaliq (the Creator), al-Bari' (the Maker), and al-Musawwir (the Fashioner) in the Quran. If these attributes were not eternal, then God would have acquired perfection later, implying deficiency in pre-eternity. Deficiency is a sign of temporality (huduth), so attributing deficiency to God would entail that God Himself is temporal, which is impossible. Nasafi then argues that if God became a Creator only at the time of creation, His praise would depend on something other than Himself, indicating need and deficiency. Need is also a mark of temporality. Moreover, if the attribute of creation is not subsisting in God's essence, He would not deserve the name 'Creator' eternally; but if it arises later, it would imply change in God, which is also a sign of temporality. The conclusion is that denying the eternity of takwin leads to absurdities such as God being temporal, dependent, and even created, which are all impossible. The final sentence encapsulates the core point: if action is possible for God, it cannot be absent except due to incapacity; since God is not incapable, takwin must be eternal.
